	<div class="article__progress-container">

		<div class="article__main-section">
			<div class="article-content">
												<div class="article-content__tag">
					<div class="article-content__tag__label">
						<span>
							Tag :
						</span>
					</div>
					<div class="article-content__tag__item">
						<div class="article-content__tag__item__badge">
							<a href="/blog/cybersecurity">Cyber Security</a>
						</div>
					</div>
									</div>
								<div class="article-content__main-content">
					<article>
						<p><img alt="Mallox Ransomware" src="/sites/default/files/inline-images/Cyber-Security/Mallox-Ransomware.jpg" /></p>

<h2><span>1. Mallox Ransomware Description</span></h2>

<p><span>In October 2021 Mallox, a new type of ransomware, began attacking enterprises in Asia. This new ransomware is identified by encrypted files being given the suffix “. mallox”.</span></p>

<p><img alt="1" src="/sites/default/files/inline-images/Cyber-Security/1.jpg" /></p>

<p><span>After Sangfor FarSight Labs Endpoint Security Team captured samples of this new malware strain, analysis found that Mallox was even more destructive than currently active ransomware.&nbsp;</span></p>

<ol>
	<li><span>Mallox adds a C# shell layer using common DLL hijacking technology to bypass security software.</span></li>
	<li><span>Mallox spread like a worm through file sharing and uses the same file retrieval technology as Search Artifact to attain rapid file retrieval and encryption.</span></li>
</ol>

<p><span>Mallox can encrypt many files in a very short period of time, resulting in irreparable losses once it is installed on a company's computers.</span></p>

<h2><span>2. Technical Analysis</span></h2>

<div><span>To bypass anti-virus software, Mallox adds a C# shell layer to hide its malicious behavior, and uses SmartAssembly to obfuscate the C# shell, as seen below:</span></div>

<p><img alt="image2" src="/sites/default/files/inline-images/Cyber-Security/image2.jpeg" /></p>

<p><span>AdvancedRun.exe is installed and run in the temp directory:</span></p>

<p><span><img alt="image3" src="/sites/default/files/inline-images/Cyber-Security/image3.jpeg" /></span></p>

<p><span>AdvancedRun.exe presents a configuration window when started:</span></p>

<p><span><img alt="image4" src="/sites/default/files/inline-images/Cyber-Security/image4.jpeg" /></span></p>

<p><span>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p><span>Windows Defender is turned off:</span></p>

<p><span><img alt="image5" src="/sites/default/files/inline-images/Cyber-Security/image5.jpeg" /></span></p>

<p><span>The Windows Defender directory is deleted:</span></p>

<p><img alt="image6" src="/sites/default/files/inline-images/Cyber-Security/image6.jpeg" /></p>

<p><span>The AdvancedRun.exe file is then deleted:</span></p>

<p><img alt="image7" src="/sites/default/files/inline-images/Cyber-Security/image7.jpeg" /></p>

<p><span>The script file Yubhigusnhbrkitykwictqkill$.bat is created in the temp directory:</span></p>

<p><span><img alt="image8" src="/sites/default/files/inline-images/Cyber-Security/image8.jpeg" /></span></p>

<p><span>The operation of the script file Yubhigusnhbrkitykwictqkill$.bat is as follows, with the main functions being:</span></p>

<ol>
	<li>Restoring the CMD default association by deleting the registry "HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Command Processor\AutoRun".</li>
	<li>Setting security permissions for specified files and folders to prevent them from becoming inaccessible: cmd.exe, net.exe, net1.exe, mshta.exe, FTP.exe, wscript.exe, cscript.exe, powershell.exe, C: \ProgramData, C:\Users\Public.</li>
	<li>Deleting the shadow disk.</li>
	<li>Stopping and deleting specific programs and services, including security software and any related to line-of-business.</li>
</ol>

<p><img alt="image9" src="/sites/default/files/inline-images/Cyber-Security/image9.jpeg" /></p>

<p><span>The Visual Basic script Blffpekna.vbs is created in the temp directory to run Yubhigusnhbrkitykwictqkill$.bat:</span></p>

<p><span><img alt="image10" src="/sites/default/files/inline-images/Cyber-Security/image10.jpeg" /></span></p>

<p><span>The Yubhigusnhbrkitykwictqkill$.bat script is run:</span></p>

<p><span><img alt="image11" src="/sites/default/files/inline-images/Cyber-Security/image11.jpeg" /></span></p>

<p><span>MSBuild.exe in the .NET installation directory is copied into the temp directory:</span></p>

<p><img alt="The New Threat: Mallox Ransomware" data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="ed9bf11a-e4b1-4682-8485-65f0064363cb" src="/sites/default/files/inline-images/12.jpg" /></p>

<p><span>The running MSBuild.exe process is identified, and the ransomware main module is injected into the MSBuild.exe process to bypass the security software:</span></p>

<p><img alt="image13" src="/sites/default/files/inline-images/Cyber-Security/image13.jpeg" /></p>

<p>The main Mallox module is an exe file that implements the encryption functions. The following prepared is done before encryption:</p>

<ol>
	<li><span>Excludes hosts in Russia, Kazakhstan, Russia, Ukraine and Qatar&nbsp;</span></li>
	<li>Elevates permissions</li>
	<li>Deletes the registration form for Raccine</li>
	<li>Deletes the disk shadow</li>
	<li>Cancels the automatic startup repair mode</li>
	<li>Terminates the following program process:</li>
</ol>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p><img alt="image14" src="/sites/default/files/inline-images/Cyber-Security/image14.jpeg" /></p>

<p><span>If a program is running under the debugger, an exception will be thrown when trying to use CloseHandle to close the handle returned by the FindFirstFile function which prevents the malware from being closed. The malware will prevent debugging from starting again:</span></p>

<p><span><img alt="image15" src="/sites/default/files/inline-images/Cyber-Security/image15.jpeg" /></span></p>

<p><span>The number of encryption threads created are 2 times the number of existing processors with an upper limit of 64 threads:</span></p>

<p><span><img alt="image16" src="/sites/default/files/inline-images/Cyber-Security/image16.jpeg" /></span></p>

<p><span>The encryption threads are synchronized using IOCP and encrypts target files found using the file traversal thread:&nbsp;</span></p>

<p><span><img alt="image17" src="/sites/default/files/inline-images/Cyber-Security/image17.jpeg" /></span></p>

<p><span>The Chacha20 algorithm (a variant of the Salsa20 stream cipher) is used to encrypt files with the encryption suffix ".mallox".</span></p>

<p><img alt="image18" src="/sites/default/files/inline-images/Cyber-Security/image18.jpeg" /></p>

<p><span>Ransom information:</span></p>

<p><img alt="The New Threat: Mallox Ransomware" data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="80cae6e4-4990-4a16-826b-06ce806a66c4" src="/sites/default/files/inline-images/image19.jpg" /></p>

<p><span>Retrieve IP addresses from the ARP table to create a virus propagation thread:</span></p>

<p><img alt="image20" src="/sites/default/files/inline-images/Cyber-Security/image20.jpeg" /></p>

<p>Name the malware file mall.exe and copy it through file sharing to the IP hosts from the ARP table, then create a corresponding service on the target systems. If the virus is run without a shell, it can be spread automatically:</p>

<p><img alt="image21" src="/sites/default/files/inline-images/Cyber-Security/image21.jpeg" /></p>

<p>Obtain system disk information of all network disks, removable disks, and local disks. Create a thread for each disk that needs to be encrypted by traversing to find files:</p>

<p><img alt="image22" src="/sites/default/files/inline-images/Cyber-Security/image22.jpeg" /></p>

<p><span>Use this method of reading USN logs to quickly retrieve disk files:</span></p>

<p><span><img alt="image23" src="/sites/default/files/inline-images/Cyber-Security/image23.jpeg" /></span></p>

<p><span>Filter out the ransomware files and the files of the program itself:</span></p>

<p><img alt="image24" src="/sites/default/files/inline-images/Cyber-Security/image24.jpeg" /></p>

<p><span>Then filter out the following suffix files:</span></p>

<p><img alt="image25" src="/sites/default/files/inline-images/Cyber-Security/image25.png" /></p>

<p><img alt="image26" src="/sites/default/files/inline-images/Cyber-Security/image26.jpeg" /></p>

<p><span>Get the full path of the files and filter the following directories:</span></p>

<p><img alt="The New Threat: Mallox Ransomware" data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="9af72d59-2a09-4f98-a685-115b9f0e0e75" src="/sites/default/files/inline-images/image27_0.png" /></p>

<p><img alt="image28" src="/sites/default/files/inline-images/Cyber-Security/image28.jpeg" /></p>

<p><span>Send eligible files to the encryption thread for file encryption:</span></p>

<p><img alt="image29" src="/sites/default/files/inline-images/Cyber-Security/image29.jpeg" /></p>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<h2><span>3. Protection Recommendations</span></h2>

<ol>
	<li><span>Set up access permissions for important files and turn off unnecessary file sharing features.</span></li>
	<li><span>Perform regular non-local (offline) backups.&nbsp;</span></li>
	<li><span>Use a highly secure host password and avoid multiple devices using the same password.</span></li>
	<li><span>Do not map ports like 3389 directly to the internet or an external network to prevent brute-force cracking.</span></li>
	<li><span>Avoid opening emails, links, and URL attachments of unknown origin.</span></li>
	<li><span>Do not download non-genuine software from unofficial sites.</span></li>
	<li><span>If you find that the file type does not match the original icon, you should scan the file using endpoint detection software to detect any malicious code within the file.&nbsp;</span></li>
	<li><span>Regularly scan the system for vulnerabilities and install patches in a timely manner.</span></li>
</ol>

<p><span>&nbsp;</span></p>

<h2><span>4. Using Sangfor Products:</span></h2>

<p><span><img alt="The New Threat: Mallox Ransomware" data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="1173575a-98c8-4136-ae3e-6e588ae6079f" src="/sites/default/files/inline-images/image30.png" />&nbsp;</span></p>

<ol>
	<li><span>Run anti-virus and vulnerability scans using Endpoint Secure.</span></li>
	<li><span>For users of Sangfor Cyber Command, NGAF, and Endpoint Secure, it is recommended that the system engines and signature databases are upgraded regularly.&nbsp;</span></li>
	<li><span>Connect to Neural-X and use Cloud Sandbox to detect and defend against new threats.</span></li>
	<li><span>Sangfor provides free bot and virus removal tools to users. You can download the virus detection and protection tools here: <a href="https://active.sangfor.com/sangfor-anti-bot-tool">https://page.sangfor.com/anti-bot-tool</a></span></li>
	<li><span>Sangfor Engine Zero malware detection engine is integrated into most Sangfor security products to provide precision defense against unknown viruses and malware.</span></li>
	<li><span>Sangfor has a suite of Security Assessment Services to help users quickly find gaps in their security architecture and develop remediation plans.</span></li>
	<li><span>Sangfor Security Assessment Services provide security device policy inspection, threat hunting &amp; detection, and vulnerability inspections to ensure that risks are immediately identified, and remediation strategies developed to prevent successful attacks in the future.</span></li>
</ol>

<script defer>function handleFormSubmit(ele) {
    var submitButton = ele.querySelector('input[type=submit]');
    var spinner = document.createElement('span');
    spinner.setAttribute('class', 'loader');
    submitButton.setAttribute('disabled', true);
    submitButton.style.cursor = 'wait';
    submitButton.parentNode.appendChild(spinner);
    return true;
  }
  function resetSubmitButton(e){
    var submitButtons = e.target.form.getElementsByClassName('submit-button');
    for(var i=0;i<submitButtons.length;i++){
      submitButtons[i].disabled = false;
    }
  }
  function addChangeHandler(elements){
    for(var i=0; i<elements.length; i++){
      elements[i].addEventListener('change', resetSubmitButton);
    }
  }
  var form = document.getElementById('form24');
  addChangeHandler(form.getElementsByTagName('input'));
  addChangeHandler(form.getElementsByTagName('select'));
  addChangeHandler(form.getElementsByTagName('textarea'));
  var nodes = document.querySelectorAll('#form24 input[data-subscription]');
  if (nodes) {
    for (var i = 0, len = nodes.length; i < len; i++) {
      var status = nodes[i].dataset ? nodes[i].dataset.subscription : nodes[i].getAttribute('data-subscription');
      if(status ==='true') {
        nodes[i].checked = true;
      }
    }
  };
  var nodes = document.querySelectorAll('#form24 select[data-value]');
  if (nodes) {
    for (var i = 0; i < nodes.length; i++) {
      var node = nodes[i];
      var selectedValue = node.dataset ? node.dataset.value : node.getAttribute('data-value');
      if (selectedValue) {
        for (var j = 0; j < node.options.length; j++) {
          if(node.options[j].value === selectedValue) {
            node.options[j].selected = 'selected';
            break;
          }
        }
      }
    }
  }
  this.getParentElement = function(list) {
    return list[list.length-1].parentElement};
  var dom0 = document.querySelector('#form24 #fe238');

    against: function(value) {

    }
    , failureMessage: "Value must not contain any URL's"}
           );
  fe238.add(Validate.Custom, {

    }
    , failureMessage: "Value must not contain any HTML"}

  fe238.add(Validate.Length, {

    failureMessage:"This field is required"}

<script defer>document.onload = handleDocumentLoad('form24','757079');
  function handleDocumentLoad(b,a){
    window.getElqFormSubmissionToken(b,a);
    window.processLastFormField()}
  function getElqFormSubmissionToken(g,c){
    var e=new XMLHttpRequest();
    var b=document.getElementById(g);
    if(b&&b.elements.namedItem("elqFormSubmissionToken")){
      var f=b.action;
      var a=window.getHostName(f);
      a="https://"+a+"/e/formsubmittoken?elqSiteID="+c;
      if(a){
        e.onreadystatechange=function(){
          if(e.readyState===4){
            if(e.status===200){
              b.elements.namedItem("elqFormSubmissionToken").value=e.responseText}
            else{
              b.elements.namedItem("elqFormSubmissionToken").value=""}
          }
        };
        e.open("GET",a,true);
        e.send()}
      else{
        b.elements.namedItem("elqFormSubmissionToken").value=""}
    }
  }
  function getHostName(b){
    if(typeof window.URL==="function"){
      return new window.URL(b).hostname}
    else{
      var a=b.match(/:\/\/(www[0-9]?\.)?(.[^\/:]+)/i);
      if(a!==null&&a.length>2&&typeof a[2]==="string"&&a[2].length>0){
        return a[2]}
      else{
        return null}
    }
  }
  function processLastFormField(){
    var form = document.getElementById("form24");
    var lastFormField = form.querySelector("#elq-FormLastRow");
    lastFormField.style.display = "none";
  }
</script>
